    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17870437588953617293"><p>There are six things very wrong with my life:<br/><br/>1.   <span id="freeText17870437588953617293" style="display:none"><p>There are six things very wrong with my life:<br /><br />1. I have one of those under-the-skin spots that will never come to a head but lurk in a red way for the next two years.<br /><br />2. It is on my nose<br /><br />3. I have a three-year-old sister who may have peed somewhere in my room.<br /><br />4. In fourteen days the summer hols will be over and then it will be back to Stalag 14 and Oberfuhrer Frau Simpson and her bunch of sadistic teachers.<br /><br />5. I am very ugly and need to go into an ugly home.<br /><br />6. I went to a party dressed as a stuffed olive.<br /></p><p><br />In this wildly funny journal of a year in the life of Georgia Nicolson, British author Louise Rennison has perfectly captured the soaring joys and bottomless angst of being a teenager. In the spirit of <i>Bridget Jones's Diary</i>, this fresh, irreverent, and simply hilarious book will leave you laughing out loud. As Georgia would say, it's "Fabbity fab fab!"</p></span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Uhm, kind of. I read the books first and watched the movie when it came out and I loved both!<br/><br/>The movie kind of only focuses on the first book (with bi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Uhm, kind of. I read the books first and watched the movie when it came out and I loved both!<br /><br />The movie kind of only focuses on the first book (with bits frankensteined in from other books) so it doesn't highlight the greatness of some of the characters (e.g. Dave the Laugh who is one of my favourites is kind of a blasé character).<br /><br />BUT, again, I love the book and the movies.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54578945" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54578945?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780641925788" href="/book/show/8286130-angus-thongs-and-full-frontal-snogging">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those in need of a good laugh</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=printz">printz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fun-and-dumb">fun-and-dumb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54578945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6117773331565827114"><b>Update 1/2/2017</b> Accidentally read it yet again. Not a bad beginning-of-the-year pick-me-up.<br/><br/><br/><br/>There are times when I just HAVE to read something to perk me up, something light and silly and mindless. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/65189.Louise_Rennison' title='Louise Rennison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Louise Rennison</a>'s books always do the trick. It doesn't hurt either that this first book in <i>Confessions of Georgia Nicolson</i> series is a winner of <i>Printz Honor</i>, proving that even the silliest story about make-up, boys, and snogging can be written brilliantly. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/563712.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_' title='Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> neve</span>
  <span id="freeText6117773331565827114" style="display:none"><b>Update 1/2/2017</b> Accidentally read it yet again. Not a bad beginning-of-the-year pick-me-up.<br /><br /><br /><br />There are times when I just HAVE to read something to perk me up, something light and silly and mindless. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/65189.Louise_Rennison" title="Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Louise Rennison</a>'s books always do the trick. It doesn't hurt either that this first book in <i>Confessions of Georgia Nicolson</i> series is a winner of <i>Printz Honor</i>, proving that even the silliest story about make-up, boys, and snogging can be written brilliantly. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/563712.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_" title="Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> never takes itself seriously or tries to teach some kind of moral lesson. Instead, its only aim is to provide tons of fun; and the book succeeds at it every time I read it. I do not think there is any point for me to sing this novel any more praise to convince you to give it a try, rather, I will list some quotes here for you to see if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/65189.Louise_Rennison" title="Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Louise Rennison</a>'s humor is your cup of tea.<br /><br /><i>Wednesday, December 2nd.<br /><br />8:30 a.m.<br />Dashing out of the house, Jas and I almost fell into Mark, waiting by the corner. Jas (big pal) said she had to run to her house first and she would see me at school. I went a bit red and walked on with him walking beside me. He said, "Have you got a boyfriend?"<br />I was speechless. What is the right answer to that question? I tell you what the right answer is... a lie, that's the right answer. So I said, "I've just come out of a heavy thing and I'm giving myself a bit of space."<br />He looked at me. He really did have the biggest gob [mouth:] I have ever seen. "So is that no?"<br />And I just stood there and then this really weird thing happened... he touched my breast!!! I don't mean he ripped my blouse off, he just rested his hand on the front of my breast. Just for a second, before he turned and went off to school.<br /><br />12:30 p.m.<br />What does it mean when a boy rests his hand on your breast? Does it mean he has a megahorn? Or was his hand just tired? <br /><br />4:30 p.m.<br />Why am I even thinking about this? No sign of Mark (the breast molester) when I got home, thank goodness.<br /><br />4:45 p.m.<br />Still, you would think if a boy rests his hand on your breast he might bother to see you sometime.<br /><br />* * *<br /><br />Sunday, February 7th<br /><br />11:00 a.m.<br /><br />Got dressed in short skirt, then me and Jas walked up and down to the main road. We wanted to see how many cars with boys in them hooted at us. Ten!! (We had to walk up and down for four hours... still, ten is ten!!!)</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6117773331565827114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12902911240450479478"><br/>So most girls, I assume, would have read this back in middle school, but *dramatically flips hair* I’m not like most girls.<br/><br/>^That was lame, I apologize. <br/><br/>Basically, the only reason I read this book is because my lovely coffee-soddened friend, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pragya</a>, who is probably trying to get back at me for some horrible thing I did but am unaware of, convinced me to. :) :)<br/><br/>This book is so terrible and I feel like I probably shouldn’t be rating it, since it’s not targeted towards me, but, <b> it’s just so <i> bad. </i> </b><br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText12902911240450479478" style="display:none"><br>So most girls, I assume, would have read this back in middle school, but *dramatically flips hair* I’m not like most girls.<br><br>^That was lame, I apologize. <br><br>Basically, the only reason I read this book is because my lovely coffee-soddened friend, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya" rel="nofollow noopener">Pragya</a>, who is probably trying to get back at me for some horrible thing I did but am unaware of, convinced me to. :) :)<br><br>This book is so terrible and I feel like I probably shouldn’t be rating it, since it’s not targeted towards me, but, <b> it’s just so <i> bad. </i> </b><br><br>The main character is the most annoying character I’ve ever read. The only thing she talks about it:<br>1.	Her nose<br>2.	Boys<br>3.	How her friends are losers<br>4.	Her nose<br>5.	And how her life sucks so much, she wants to die<br><br>I’ve never seen a fourteen-year old act like this, this is a terrible representation of teenagers, y’all should be <b> ashamed! </b><br><br>And the humour felt so <i> forced. </i> It wasn’t even funny. <br><br><i> How do people like this book???!!! </i><br><br>And WHY is there 10 books in the series???!! TEN BOOKS???!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480772246ra/21348556.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So . . . I’m sorry if you’re offended, or if this book was your early teenage happiness but the only reason I wrote such a terrible review was for the crazy coffee lover I mentioned earlier. <br><br>So there, I hope you’re happy, you’ve made me do a terrible thing. <br><br><br><i> “I suppose this is what life will be like for me—never having a boyfriend, always just living through others” </i><br><br><br>1 star!!<br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13160344310448507106">Hillariosity! This is another book, from the brits, that people either love or hate. I happen to love this series, and laughed so hard I actually cried. I think people who hate this book are turned off by the main character Georgia. She is vain, self centered, hormonal, ridiculous and, I think, absolutely fabulous. This is the first of a series and we are introduced to her mad little sister libby, her feral cat Angus, her Mum and Dad, and group of silly girlfriends. It's written as a diary and a</span>
  <span id="freeText13160344310448507106" style="display:none">Hillariosity! This is another book, from the brits, that people either love or hate. I happen to love this series, and laughed so hard I actually cried. I think people who hate this book are turned off by the main character Georgia. She is vain, self centered, hormonal, ridiculous and, I think, absolutely fabulous. This is the first of a series and we are introduced to her mad little sister libby, her feral cat Angus, her Mum and Dad, and group of silly girlfriends. It's written as a diary and a lot of people like to compare it to Bridget Jones. I have never read Bridget Jones so I can't really comment on that. I can however say that I took this book with me on a trip and illicited many curious glances from strangers in the airport. They may have thought I was having a seizure, but in fact I as laughing my bum off. </span>

<div id="review_985060864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/985060864" />
    <a title="Aly (In Wonderland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22178203-aly-in-wonderland"><img alt="Aly (In Wonderland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552929589p2/22178203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/985060864?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (In Wonderland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (In Wonderland)" href="/user/show/22178203-aly-in-wonderland">Aly (In Wonderland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer985060864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9681844333481091601"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410650945ra/11136358.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410650945i/11136359.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410650945ra/11136360.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410650945ra/11136361.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This book was my bible back in '08.</b><br/><br/>Seriously. My friends and I would refer to <i>this book</i> whenever we had something that could be considered as "boy problems". In '08, I was 13/14, and I'd fallen in love with Aaron Johnson after watching the film so, of course, I had to read the book.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer960622505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6927496611634578414">*Sigh* I wanted fluff, not brain-damage. Based on the recommendation from several friends who loved this, I picked this up when I saw it at a library sale, and I figured that now was a good time to read it since I'd just read a duo of emotionally traumatizing books and needed something light and fun after that. <br/><br/>But this, aside from having a few funny moments, was mostly a 14 year old selfish angst-fest. If I was that annoying as a 14 year old, I think I may have to nominate my parents for sainth</span>
  <span id="freeText6927496611634578414" style="display:none">*Sigh* I wanted fluff, not brain-damage. Based on the recommendation from several friends who loved this, I picked this up when I saw it at a library sale, and I figured that now was a good time to read it since I'd just read a duo of emotionally traumatizing books and needed something light and fun after that. <br /><br />But this, aside from having a few funny moments, was mostly a 14 year old selfish angst-fest. If I was that annoying as a 14 year old, I think I may have to nominate my parents for sainthood for not murdering me. I got so bored with it by the middle that I ended up skimming most of the second half. Drama, boys, makeup, snotty fucking "sense of humor" and cattiness. Thank god I'm not a teenager anymore. <br /><br />I wasn't a fan of the style of this book either. It was written in journal format, but as is often the case, it ends up being mostly 1st person. But being that Miss Georgia is a drama queen, I can forgive that. She'd want to pour her heart out. But damn it was choppy and random and the timestamps didn't make sense. I think a lot of them were supposed to be funny, like "Oh, I'm going to do this thing and it's going to make me look like a fashion model and then the Sex God will love me!" and then 2 minutes later, "My life is ruined!" <br /><br />Ha ha ha. See how funny that was? Yeah. Me neither. 2 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6927496611634578414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30271533" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1002184-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1206657855p2/1002184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30271533?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1002184-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1002184-sara?shelf=ya-fiction-girly">ya-fiction-girly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1002184-sara?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30271533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9229225701569059763">I got to the point where I couldn't read this book during silent reading time in my class, it made me laugh so hard. I'm not an easy touch for this type of humor - slapstick and outrageous. ATFFS, however, made me laugh so hard, I snorted. The epistolary nature of the narrative adds so much to the plot. A snippet about a girl who accidentally-on-purpose shaves off her eyebrows is cringingly amusing, but when it's told in five or six installments, each a few minutes apart, and that snippet weaves</span>
  <span id="freeText9229225701569059763" style="display:none">I got to the point where I couldn't read this book during silent reading time in my class, it made me laugh so hard. I'm not an easy touch for this type of humor - slapstick and outrageous. ATFFS, however, made me laugh so hard, I snorted. The epistolary nature of the narrative adds so much to the plot. A snippet about a girl who accidentally-on-purpose shaves off her eyebrows is cringingly amusing, but when it's told in five or six installments, each a few minutes apart, and that snippet weaves itself through the rest of the narrative in little comments like, "No news on the eyebrow front," there's no way to avoid laughing until your stomach aches. The fact of the matter is that Georgia is a tragic hero. You couldn't laugh so much if there wasn't something inherently tragic about her inability to enjoy life and admit it. She throws herself into frays in which it is obvious that she will be destroyed, and we cheer her on because she keeps trying. Georgia is who we want to be, because she succeeds through ridiculous perseverance. Read it and laugh, because weeping isn't far behind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9229225701569059763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12897879142373013948">I've wanted to read this book since I was about 12 years old and somehow I never got around to it. Unfortunately, at 28 years of age I am well, <i>well</i> beyond Georgia Nicolson's target audience.<br/><br/>This is a very silly book that hasn't aged well. There are lot of jokes made at the expense of the LGBT community right off the bat. Which of course back then was seen as harmless, but imagine how a young struggling gay teen might feel reading Georgia's pleas of "oh God please, please don't make me have to b</span>
  <span id="freeText12897879142373013948" style="display:none">I've wanted to read this book since I was about 12 years old and somehow I never got around to it. Unfortunately, at 28 years of age I am well, <i>well</i> beyond Georgia Nicolson's target audience.<br /><br />This is a very silly book that hasn't aged well. There are lot of jokes made at the expense of the LGBT community right off the bat. Which of course back then was seen as harmless, but imagine how a young struggling gay teen might feel reading Georgia's pleas of "oh God please, please don't make me have to be a lesbian like <i>Hairy Kate.</i>" Hairy Kate! Because we all know lesbians are abominable snowmen posing as women. <br /><br />Anyway Georgia is terribly boring and whiny - weren't we all? She makes a lot of jokes about suicide, how ugly she is, and how shallow her friends are (grab a mirror, babe). It's maybe exactly the way a thirteen year-old would act but it's very much an early 2000s book that I think can probably be left there. Teens need better role models than Georgia.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7589403-lydia?shelf=tween-reads">tween-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271168397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer504937253754303661">Think Diary of a Wimpy Kid for tweens, without the illustrations, and one can pretty much have an accurate idea of what this book is about. Although critically acclaimed and with awards to its name (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.harpercollins.com/books/Angus-Thongs-Full-Frontal-Snogging-Louise-Rennison/?isbn=9780064472272'>http://www.harpercollins.com/books/An...</a>) I would personally re-title this book "Diary of a Petty, Shallow Tween."<br/><br/>Now, don't misunderstand me. I laughed out loud at portions of the story, and most definitely felt as if I was reading the actual diary of quite a few of the tweens and young teens I work</span>
  <span id="freeText504937253754303661" style="display:none">Think Diary of a Wimpy Kid for tweens, without the illustrations, and one can pretty much have an accurate idea of what this book is about. Although critically acclaimed and with awards to its name (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.harpercollins.com/books/Angus-Thongs-Full-Frontal-Snogging-Louise-Rennison/?isbn=9780064472272">http://www.harpercollins.com/books/An...</a>) I would personally re-title this book "Diary of a Petty, Shallow Tween."<br /><br />Now, don't misunderstand me. I laughed out loud at portions of the story, and most definitely felt as if I was reading the actual diary of quite a few of the tweens and young teens I work with regularly. However I would argue that the narrative is a reflection of a popular perception, but in reality a narrow representation of "tweendome" as we know it today.<br /><br />Set in England (with a glossary in the back for us "American-type chums"), the character of Georgia Nicolson can be summed up in the following quotes:<br />1. "I have no friends. Not one single friend. No one has rung, no one has come around...I may as well be dead."<br />2. "I love my life! Jas has just phoned to say we've been invited to a party..."<br />3. "the only way I will believe in God is if something really bloody great happens to me soon."<br /><br />The emotional rollercoaster of a protagonist alternates between highs and lows, detests her family most of the time, is obsessed with boys and "snogging" (aka "kissing" -- even to the point of visiting a professional snogger in order to learn the art) and is completely self-absorbed in an immature, comedic way.<br /><br />Which, in reality, does describe the life of a typical tween. However, although every tween girl surely does experience these emotions and will be able to identify with the character, the extreme level of Georgia's shallowness will frustrate many. Young girls with socially conservative or religious backgrounds (who see relationships between the opposite sex as a serious matter, not something to be traded around like a baseball card), or girls who are involved in sports, the arts and academics (giving them a goal to strive for rather than finding their identity solely in their popularity) may not enjoy this book.<br /><br />Over-all, a good look into the life of a tween, being an enthralling read for tweens that may identify, and the laugh-out-loud hilarity give it high marks, but there are also tweens (and parents) who may strongly dislike the loose morals and shallowness of the main character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="504937253754303661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11129640402823050386">Let me just start this review by saying I love this book. LOVE IT! This is one of the few books that I've really, truly laughed out loud while reading - there were times I was seriously doubled over. It is hilarious. I'm going to start recommending this book to everyone I know. <br/><br/>But, just so you know, this book is strictly a fun read, nothing more (still well worth reading, believe me). <br/><br/>Georgia Nicolson is a self-centered fourteen-year-old girl growing up in England. Her story is told through her</span>
  <span id="freeText11129640402823050386" style="display:none">Let me just start this review by saying I love this book. LOVE IT! This is one of the few books that I've really, truly laughed out loud while reading - there were times I was seriously doubled over. It is hilarious. I'm going to start recommending this book to everyone I know. <br /><br />But, just so you know, this book is strictly a fun read, nothing more (still well worth reading, believe me). <br /><br />Georgia Nicolson is a self-centered fourteen-year-old girl growing up in England. Her story is told through her daily (-ish) journal entries: all about her fourth year (the equivalent of ninth grade here in the States) at her all-girl school. <br /><br />She rambles on about anything and everything that crosses her mind: boys, clothing, snogging, pranks, her "inept parents", her little sister, said little sisters nappies (and how they sometimes explode or get left in her room), her monstrous cat, and knickers. While her thoughts aren't in the least bit deep - quite the opposite, really - they are quite hilarious. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_178754819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178754819" />
    <a title="Lena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5289798-lena"><img alt="Lena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303234650p2/5289798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178754819?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena" href="/user/show/5289798-lena">Lena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who likes to laugh</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289798-lena?shelf=love-of-learning">love-of-learning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289798-lena?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289798-lena?shelf=lol">lol</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178754819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3246699711925163184">Second reading, 10 years later (original review below).<br/>Okay, so I read this book quite a while ago, and IDK if I'm just more socially aware now, but OMG this book has some really... questionable...things. I can't imagine it being published today. There's some very casual homophobia--Georgia is always worrying that her gym teacher, whom she says is a lesbian, is checking her out. She casually/jokingly mentions suicide a number of times. Etc. However, I think teenagers would love it, because here'</span>
  <span id="freeText3246699711925163184" style="display:none">Second reading, 10 years later (original review below).<br />Okay, so I read this book quite a while ago, and IDK if I'm just more socially aware now, but OMG this book has some really... questionable...things. I can't imagine it being published today. There's some very casual homophobia--Georgia is always worrying that her gym teacher, whom she says is a lesbian, is checking her out. She casually/jokingly mentions suicide a number of times. Etc. However, I think teenagers would love it, because here's the thing. I have a teenager, and this is exactly what they are like--not all, of course, but lots of them are not politically correct and imbue serious issues with the gravitas adults do. They're flippant and irreverent and have zero interest in a lecture. And they'd probably appreciate a refreshingly honest book like this, where there's no great lesson/moral/lecture about the evils of making suicide jokes or anything like that. I didn't even notice those things when I read this as a young adult, so maybe it was just part of the way I talked at the time, too. Nothing wrong with growing older and wiser, but it was definitely not the light-hearted romp I remember.<br /><br />First reading review:<br />This is the funniest book I've ever read. It's the journal of Georgia Nicholson, who is often on the rack of lurve. The book is British, and has lots of odd British humor, but plenty of humor that will make even the most curmudgeonly person laugh their butt off. I can't think of a single person who would not find at least part of this book hilarious. I've never laughed so hard at a book in my life. At one point I laughed so hard someone asked me why I was crying. I'm pretty sure I actually rolled on the floor laughing at one point. <br />I can't think of anything to say about this book other than it's hilarious, refreshing, and amazing. Recommended to anyone who has a sense of humor or wishes they did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3246699711925163184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2098381-heather">Heather</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780064472272" href="/book/show/563712.Angus_Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Heather by: </span>
      T
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72754305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12667096277671399271">This book is laugh out loud funny! The proper English slang took some getting used to, but luckily the author has included a glossary in the back.<br/><br/>Georgia is full of hilariosity and she along with her Ace Gang, mad sister, and fat vati will have you laughing like a loon on loon tablets. Gee is neither kind nor cruel, smart nor intelligent, but witty she is and she is forever getting herself into a jam due to her neurotic nature and obsession with boys, make up and hair.<br/><br/>Angus, Thongs, and Full Fro</span>
  <span id="freeText12667096277671399271" style="display:none">This book is laugh out loud funny! The proper English slang took some getting used to, but luckily the author has included a glossary in the back.<br /><br />Georgia is full of hilariosity and she along with her Ace Gang, mad sister, and fat vati will have you laughing like a loon on loon tablets. Gee is neither kind nor cruel, smart nor intelligent, but witty she is and she is forever getting herself into a jam due to her neurotic nature and obsession with boys, make up and hair.<br /><br />Angus, Thongs, and Full Frontal Snogging won't enrich your life. It's not meaningful, unless its serves as a trumpeter for individuality, you won't learn life lessons, but it's great for a laugh and serves as a reminder of how silly and daft we females once were. Enjoyable book!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12667096277671399271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1572108181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16043028752964232132">One of my favorite series! In middle school, I had to take a Sharpie to my copy of ON THE BRIGHT SIDE, I'M NOW THE GIRLFRIEND OF A SEX GOD and mark out "SEX" so I wouldn't be mortified reading at the dinner table. However, Rennison is so funny that I snorted my food and mortification was inevitable. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7jfXG2+lZo5yHxlEaESdlCfYwUSpo+WkLSn97GqDI/v+he/a0PkoPjt25MfZI6rmktfngJiUvIu30jzfW/rM9A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I9Y6D8jf8zILOy8oeMqDOSimlePELa1FvoyRPrdt5IczZALOd4O9gkJS0qvJrbRLnamzJ/Ua9Gokd1ANhhQLiA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer6382473052970044626">Louise Rennison was the bestselling award-winning author of the phenomenally successful ‘Confessions of Georgia Nicolson’ series, translated into over 34 languages and to the stage and big screen as ‘Angus, Thongs and Perfect Snogging’. She has won the Nestle Smarties Book Prize, the Michael L. Printz Honor Book and the Roald Dahl Funny prize for ‘Withering Tights’. Louise sadly died on the Februa</span>
  <span id="freeText6382473052970044626" style="display:none">Louise Rennison was the bestselling award-winning author of the phenomenally successful ‘Confessions of Georgia Nicolson’ series, translated into over 34 languages and to the stage and big screen as ‘Angus, Thongs and Perfect Snogging’. She has won the Nestle Smarties Book Prize, the Michael L. Printz Honor Book and the Roald Dahl Funny prize for ‘Withering Tights’. Louise sadly died on the February 29, 2016.<br /></span>

Now fans of Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging -- Georgia\'s first set of hilarious musings on life -- can get another peek into the mind of this wryly inquisitive English lass in the appealing sequel: On the Bright Side, I\'m Now the Girlfriend of a Sex God.\n\nAs the title implies, Georgia has snagged herself a sex god in the form of Robbie, the boy of her dreams. Now that they\'ve indulged in a bit of &quot;full-frontal snogging,&quot; Georgia turns her attention to advancing the relationship. But things quickly go wrong when she learns that her father\'s new job may necessitate a move to New Zealand. Crestfallen, Georgia feels her life might as well be over. Then, miraculously, the dreaded move is cancelled, and things seem to be getting better -- at least until 17-year-old Robbie decides to break up with Georgia because he\'s bothered by the difference in their ages. \n\nBorrowing freely from her mum\'s closet and advice books, even as she\'s steadfastly discounting everything her mum says, a crushed but determined Georgia comes up with a scheme to win Robbie back. As usual, nothing goes as planned, and life is further complicated by Georgia\'s temperamental cat, Angus (who\'s having a few amorous leanings of his own), and her baby sister, Libby, whose fascination with (and lack of control over) her bodily functions leads to several intriguing mishaps. Of course, there are other disasters, too: a quick-tan lotion that turns Georgia\'s legs orange, a run-in with the aptly named Bummer sisters, and friends who insist on focusing on their own problems from time to time.\n\nWho knew the angst of adolescence could be so much fun? This Georgia\'s-eye view of teenage life is wonderfully egocentric and side-splittingly funny. And despite the occasional language barrier (a glossary of terms is provided in the back of the book), Georgia\'s thoughts and experiences will prove universally recognizable to anyone who is, or has
